It\u2019s the sort of marquee matchup that has brought out the very best of Harden this season. Even with his 3-point shooting numbers taking a slight dip since the All-Star break (.333 in the seven games since compared to .384 in the 50 games before) Harden continues to generate offense at will for himself and everyone else. It certainly helps to have another elite point guard in Chris Paul rolling with him. They\u2019re averaging a shade under 50 points and 17 assists combined, which should come in handy with Toronto\u2019s All-Star backcourt of DeMar DeRozan and Kyle Lowry just as eager for tonight\u2019s superstar matchup. The truth is the Rockets have been the undisputed best in the business for a while now ( 24-2 since Jan. 8th and a ridiculous 34-1 with Harden, Paul and Clint Capela in the lineup this season). It all starts and ends with Harden playing at a MVP-level from the the opening tip of opening night and all the way through to the finish. Last week:  No. 2 Season stats:  27.0 points, 9.0 assists, 8.4 rebounds The Cavaliers finally knocked off a team with a .500 or better record Wednesday in Denver, thanks in large part to LeBron\u2019s finishing kick ( he scored Cleveland\u2019s final nine points on 4-for-4 shooting ). He finished with 39 points, 10 assists and eight rebounds, collecting his 24th game of the season with 30 or more points. There is a reason LeBron does not fear the competition in the Eastern Conference playoff field, not after seven straight seasons of smoking the competition when it matters most. No matter what the Toronto Raptors, Boston Celtics or any other team brings to the party, he knows he\u2019s the most impactful player on the floor every single night. (There\u2019s a reason fans in Philadelphia and Los Angeles have already ramped up their recruiting efforts in advance of this summer\u2019s sure-to-be-crazy free-agent frenzy.) That said, LeBron still has some work to do fine-tuning things with the deadline additions ( Larry Nance Jr. in the starting lineup now ) and the eventual return of All-Star power forward Kevin Love at some point. There is still plenty of room for improvement and time to get it done. Last week:  No. 3 Season stats:  25.9 points, 6.7 rebounds, 5.4 assists Durant was at his MVP-best in the Warriors\u2019 comeback win over the San Antonio Spurs Thursday night . He scored a game-high 37 points, including 14 straight down the stretch, to carry the Warriors back from an eight-point deficit in the fourth quarter. He shot 14-for-26 from the floor, 4-for-7 from deep and added 11 rebounds, four assists and four blocks on a night when Stephen Curry was lost for the night in the first quarter with another sprained ankle and both Andre Iguodala and David West were already out of the lineup nursing injuries. With Curry already ruled out for tonight\u2019s matchup against a surging Portland team at the Moda Center, the Warriors will need much more of the same from Durant, who is averaging 39 points on .538 shooting this season vs. Portland . Durant\u2019s well positioned to make a late-season push in this race, but the Warriors have more pressing matters trying to catch the Houston Rockets in the race for No. 1 in the Western Conference. Last week:  No. 6 Season stats:  26.7 points, 6.4 assists, 5.3 rebounds DeRozan put on a show (42 points, six assists) in Wednesday\u2019s win against Detroit , the Raptors\u2019 sixth straight win and the All-Star\u2019s fourth 40-point game of the season. DeRozan is averaging 25 points on .510 shooting during that streak, which is on the line tonight at Air Canada Centre with the Houston Rockets (17 straight wins of their own) visiting for a showdown between the league\u2019s top two teams in the standings. The Raptors have won 13 of their last 14 games, and continue to thrive when DeRozan has it going offensively (they are 13-2 this season when he scores 30 or more points ). And yet it was his playmaking, as well his scoring prowess, that helped the Raptors become the first team in the league to clinch a playoff berth with that win over the Pistons. His final assist in that game came when he drove in, collapsed the defense and found Fred VanVleet on the baseline for what turned out to be the game-winning jumper . His trust in his teammates, regardless of their status, is one of the key ingredients in the Raptors\u2019 success. Coach Dwane Casey\u2019s revamping of the offense wouldn\u2019t have been possible without a complete buy in from both members (Kyle Lowry, of course, being the other) of his All-Star backcourt. And it\u2019s clear that they are all in. The Atlanta Hawks have made the playoffs in each of the last 10 seasons , while the Memphis Grizzlies have done it in each of the last seven . Currently, those two teams sit in last place in their respective conferences . The fourth-longest active streak, the six-year run belonging to the LA Clippers , is also in danger of coming to an end. But just how safe is the the *third longest playoff streak in NBA history? The San Antonio Spurs have reached the postseason in each of the last 20 seasons and currently sit in fifth place in the Western Conference. * The record belongs to the Philadelphia 76ers, who were in the postseason in each of their first 22 seasons (14 as the Syracuse Nationals), from 1950-71 . The second longest streak (21 seasons) belongs to the Portland Trail Blazers ( 1983-2003 ). In fifth place, the Spurs are just three games in the loss column ahead of the ninth-place Denver Nuggets. The Spurs are 3-8 since Feb. 1 , they\u2019ve lost seven of their last eight games against teams that currently have winning records, and they\u2019ll be playing a lot more of those teams over the final five weeks of the season. In regard to opponent strength, the Spurs have the league\u2019s toughest remaining schedule, with 15 of their 18 remaining games against teams that currently have winning records. One of the other games is on the road against the Los Angeles Lakers, who are 18-8 over the last two months and just beat the Spurs (in San Antonio) on Saturday . The Spurs have four games remaining (two apiece) against the Golden State Warriors and Houston Rockets. The first of those is Thursday in Oakland, the second game of Thursday\u2019s TNT double-header ( 10:30 p.m. ET ). * Schuhmann:  Critical time in East playoff chase, too Trying to figure out if the Spurs could possibly miss the playoffs requires predicting what\u2019s going to happen in the 113 games remaining that involve the eight teams currently sitting between third and 10th place in the West. The playoff picture in the Western Conference is a wild scrum and making sense of it is probably an impossible task. We\u2019ll do our best \u2026 If the standings were based on per-game point differential, the Spurs would still be in third place in the West . They\u2019re 37-27 with the point differential of a team that\u2019s 40-24. The Oklahoma City Thunder (37-29 with the point differential of a team that\u2019s 40-26), Utah Jazz (35-30 with the point differential of a team that\u2019s 38-27) and Minnesota Timberwolves (38-28 with the point differential of a team that\u2019s 40-26) have also been better than their record. The New Orleans Pelicans (38-26 with the point differential of a team that\u2019s 34-30) are on the opposite end of the spectrum. If you take the records of these eight teams (the games they\u2019ve won so far) and use their point differentials to project how they\u2019ll do over the final five weeks of the season (ignoring strength of schedule), we\u2019d have a three-way tie for fourth place, the Jazz would grab the No. 8 seed, and the Nuggets and Clippers would be heading to the Lottery \u2026  The Portland Trail Blazers have won eight straight games to climb from sixth to third in the West. The New Orleans Pelicans have won 10 straight games to climb from ninth to fourth. The Blazers have ranked second defensively over the course of their streak , allowing just 97 points per 100 possessions. The streak includes wins over the No. 1 and No. 3-ranked offenses, though the Timberwolves (the No. 3 offense) were without Jimmy Butler and the streak includes twice as many wins over bottom-10 offenses (four) as top-10 offenses (two). But while the defensive numbers need that context, the streak still includes wins over the Warriors, Jazz (ending their 11-game winning streak), Wolves and Thunder. The Pelicans have been more balanced, with the eighth-ranked offense and seventh-ranked defense over the course of their streak, which includes seven road wins. But only four of the 10 wins have been over teams with winning records and the best of those opponents was the Spurs, who have not been playing well of late. So the Pelicans\u2019 streak is longer, but over their streak, the Blazers have beat tougher opponents on average. Both teams are home for most of the next two weeks, but the Blazers host the Warriors again on Friday and Anthony Davis\u2019 ankle injury (suffered in their win in Sacramento on Wednesday ) could derail the Pelicans.  While the Blazers and Pelicans are two of the four West teams that haven\u2019t lost since the All-Star break , the Nuggets (3-4), Wolves (2-3) and Spurs (2-3) are three of the seven West teams with losing records since the break. Minnesota (from fourth to sixth) and San Antonio (from third to fifth) have each slipped two spots in the standings since the break, going from having home-court advantage in the first round to playing Game 1 on the road. The Nuggets, meanwhile, have slipped from sixth to ninth. There\u2019s plenty of time to recover, but the Wolves could be without Jimmy Butler for the rest of the regular season . They\u2019re 4-6 without him, with the numbers of the league\u2019s worst defense (114 points allowed per 100 possessions) in those 10 games. In this latest absence , they\u2019ve been able to beat the two bad teams they\u2019ve played (Chicago and Sacramento), but they\u2019ve lost important games in Portland and in Utah. The Nuggets beat the Spurs in their first game out of the break, but have since lost four of their last six , losing at home to the Clippers in a game they led by 19 points in the third quarter, and losing to the Dallas Mavericks on Tuesday. Denver ranks last defensively (115 points allowed per 100 possessions) since Feb. 1 . The Spurs still rank second defensively overall , but 17th since Feb. 1. Their offense has been inconsistent all season and it\u2019s still not clear if and when they\u2019ll get Kawhi Leonard back. The Blazers have a relatively tough schedule in regard to opponent strength, with 13 of their final 17 games against teams with winning records, including three games against Golden State and Houston. They\u2019ll also play five of their seven remaining games within this group on the road. So that 3 seed is far from sewn up. The Pelicans have the most home-heavy remaining schedule in the league, with 12 of their final 18 games at the Smoothie King Center. That includes four of their six remaining games against the other seven teams in this group. But location hasn\u2019t meant much to the Pels this season. They have both a better record and a better point differential on the road (21-14, plus-1.2 per game) than at home (17-12, plus-0.7) . As noted above, the Spurs have the league\u2019s toughest remaining schedule, with 15 of their 18 games against teams with winning records and another against the improved Lakers. And Thursday\u2019s game at Golden State is just the start of a three-game trip that also includes visits to Oklahoma City (Saturday) and Houston (Monday). But that\u2019s followed by a six-game homestand, in which they\u2019ll host important games against the Pelicans, Wolves and Jazz, with a *rest advantage against Utah. * Rest advantage = When your opponent played the day before, but you did not. Over the last two seasons, home teams are 290-159 (.646) with a rest advantage and road teams are 86-82 (.512) with a rest advantage. The Timberwolves have one of the easier remaining schedules in the West, as well as more games at home than on the road, where they are 2-13 in 2018 . But we\u2019re going to know a lot about their ability to hang on without Butler in the next two weeks, because they play their next six games against teams with winning records. The Thunder have the group\u2019s fifth toughest schedule in regard to opponent strength, but after they play three of their next four games against teams with losing records, they\u2019ll play 11 straight against teams currently over .500, a stretch that includes visits to Toronto, Boston and Houston. They will play four of their six remaining games within this group (including Saturday\u2019s game against the Spurs) at home. The Clippers have a similarly tough schedule, with 15 of their 19 remaining games against teams with winning records, as well as a game against those Lakers (on the last night of the season). The Clips have just one game remaining against the top two teams in the West (at Houston next Thursday), but also visit the Toronto Raptors, who have the league\u2019s best home record , as they play nine of 11 on the road from March 13-30. The Nuggets have the most road-heavy remaining schedule of the group, with 10 of their final 17 games on the road and a seven-game, 14-day trip starting March 17. And among these teams, playing a home has been most important to the Nuggets, who have been 8.9 points per 100 possessions better at the Pepsi Center (plus-4.3) than they\u2019ve been on the road (minus-4.6) . But the Nuggets have a relatively easy schedule in regard to opponent strength. And the time to turn things around is right now. Denver will play six of its next seven games against teams that are currently under .500 (though that includes two games against the Lakers), before finishing the season with 10 straight games against teams that currently have winning records. The Jazz are one of two Western Conference teams (Dallas is the other) with more games remaining against teams that are under .500 (nine) than against teams that are over .500 (eight). They\u2019ve won their last eight games against the bad teams. The Jazz have nine of their 17 remaining games at home, but four of their five remaining games against the other teams within this group are on the road. Of course, while they still have the league\u2019s sixth biggest home-road NetRtg differential ( 7.2 points per 100 possessions ), the Jazz have won nine straight on the road . Also, their final game against the Clippers (April 5) is in Utah, and a win would clinch the tiebreaker against the Clips. There are 28 season series between these eight teams. And 11 of the head-to-head tiebreakers have been determined, with each of the eight teams having clinched at least one\u2026 Also, though the Jazz could tie the season series when they play in Minnesota on April 1, the Wolves have clinched that tiebreaker, because Utah (6-8 within the Northwest Division) can\u2019t catch Minnesota (9-4) in division record. Three more series are done with no head-to-head tiebreaker determined, because the teams split their four games \u2026 So the tiebreaker is still yet to be determined in 13 of the 28 matchups, and there are still 25 remaining games between the eight teams, starting with Spurs-Thunder on Saturday. Below are the seven head-to-head games in the next two weeks (through March 22), a critical stretch for both the Spurs and Clippers, who each play in three of the seven games. The Nuggets are the only team that isn\u2019t involved, as they\u2019re about to play five straight games against teams with losing records \u2026 (RA) \u2013 Rest advantage After head-to-head, the next tiebreaker is division winner over non-division winner. The Rockets and Warriors are set to win the Southwest and Pacific Divisions, respectively, but the door is open for one of the five Northwest Division teams to grab a tiebreaker over the Clippers, Pelicans or Spurs if that particular series finished with a 2-2 tie. Six weeks earlier, the certain first-round NBA Draft pick had roughed up the Aztecs for a school-record 44 points, making 15 of 21 shots from the floor and 7-for-10 from 3-point range in an 84-81 victory. When the Mountain West Conference adversaries played again in San Diego, suffice it to say the Aztecs weren\u2019t going to let Hutchison go off again. They double-teamed him constantly, and the three other players who weren\u2019t specifically assigned to shadow Hutchison kept close tabs on him, too. \u201cEvery time he got the ball there were five sets of eyes on him, and that makes it tough,\u201d Boise State coach Leon Rice said after the game. Not surprisingly, Hutchison made just 4-for-14 from the floor and Boise State lost 72-64. There were several other sets of eyes on Hutchison that night \u2014 34 NBA scouts attended the game. And though San Diego State\u2019s suffocating defense meant the scouts weren\u2019t treated to Hutchison\u2019s best offensive work \u2014 he scored 18 points with the help of a 10-for-15 effort at the free-throw line \u2014 they nevertheless saw plenty to fill their notebooks. Once again displaying the versatility that attracted that much NBA attention in the first place, Hutchison contributed nine rebounds, five assists and a steal. Hutchison has come a long way in two years, when Rice, after Hutchison\u2019s underwhelming sophomore season, scribbled in a notebook that he was making it a priority to help the player \u201cdiscover his hidden treasures.\u201d Rice laughs at the recollection of that particular journal entry. \u201cYou never know what [players] see in themselves,\u201d he said. \u201cThat\u2019s what I saw in him. I saw that he had all these tools to reach the potential that he\u2019s reached now. Oh my God, it\u2019s all there. He had all these things that you can\u2019t teach. I felt like if we could teach him some other things that he didn\u2019t have, we\u2019d have something special.\u201d Rice had a plan to help Hutchinson tap into that potential. Over the years he had become friends with Phil Beckner, who, as an assistant coach at Weber State, was credited with helping turn Damian Lillard into a lottery pick and NBA star. Rice wanted Beckner \u2014 who by then was working in player development for the Oklahoma City Thunder \u2014 to join his staff. His sales pitch was irresistible to an X and O, workout junkie like Beckner. Rice had another Lillard in the rough in Hutchison \u2014 a long, athletic, cerebral player who needed some fine-tuning and the motivation to make changes in order to realize his potential and become a star. Beckner jumped at the opportunity. He recalls his first workout session with Hutchison. \u201cI saw a kid oozing with potential,\u201d Beckner said. \u201cHe had so many tools and so many gifts that hadn\u2019t been tapped into yet. What I saw was this big, tall, long athletic kid who was ready to be molded into a great player.\u201d Hutchison\u2019s recollection of that day differs a bit, more than likely because of the culture shock he experienced. Not that Rice, a disciple of Gonzaga coach Mark Few and a good coach in his own right, hadn\u2019t put Hutchison through his paces. But this was different. \u201cI\u2019d just met [Beckner], and he\u2019s telling me I\u2019ve got to do this and do that,\u201d Hutchison said. \u201cAnd I\u2019m like, hold up, who is this guy? Is what he\u2019s telling me to do going to work?\u201d It didn\u2019t take long for Hutchison and Beckner to bond, and once trust had been established, Hutchison was ready to go to work. He developed what he called a \u201cno choice,\u201d mindset. In other words, Hutchison had no Plan B. It was the NBA or bust. Beckner noticed early that Hutchison\u2019s work ethic wasn\u2019t where it needed to be, not if he wanted to play in the NBA. Once Hutchison made that commitment to do whatever it took, Beckner developed a plan. \u201cHe was skinny kid,\u201d Beckner said. \u201cHe didn\u2019t play with a lot of force. So we worked on strength of force and movement with his footwork and ball handling. We mastered finishing around the basket. And then the other component, which you\u2019re seeing this year, he\u2019s become a better shooter.\u201d Hutchison made a huge jump from his sophomore year \u2014 when he averaged 6.8 points, 4.1 rebounds and 1.3 assists and shot .231 percent from 3 \u2014 to his junior season, when those numbers climbed to 17.4, 7.8, 2.6 and .377. In 2017-18, Hutchison had continued to make subtle improvements. His scoring average is up (19.8), but so are his assists (3.5). \u201cThe rate he improves at is unbelievable,\u201d Beckner said. \u201cWhat he\u2019s done in two years is crazy.\u201d Beckner points to a play Hutchison made in a 73-71 win at New Mexico in early February as evidence that total transformation has been achieved. Boise State had to rally in the second half, but Hutchison didn\u2019t feel compelled to be a one-man show. Late in the game, he moved around a high ball screen, but instead of driving into a couple of Lobo defenders, he spotted teammate Chris Sengfelder, a 6-foot-9, 246-pound power forward, alone at the 3-point line and threw him a crisp pass. Sengfelder, a .381 3-point shooter, jumped up and made a critical basket. \u201cChandler could have forced it to the rack, but he had three bodies in front of him,\u201d Beckner said. \u201cHe\u2019s seeing that, every night, the whole defense is loaded up to stop him. So instead of making the wrong play, he made the right play. If we don\u2019t hit that 3, we don\u2019t win the game.\u201d Plays like that are what have endeared Hutchison to scouts. He doesn\u2019t project to a limited role in the NBA. He\u2019s got the entire package. \u201cHe\u2019s got great size and a point guard\u2019s feel for the game,\u201d Rice said. \u201cPeople are surprised that he\u2019s bigger than they think when they stand next to him. That kind of size, coupled with feel, add in his other skills \u2026 everybody [NBA scouts] loves him.\u201d Hutchison\u2019s work with Beckner has provided an added benefit. During the summer, he gets to train with Lillard, and witness, as Beckner puts it, what it\u2019s like to be a \u201cfreak worker.\u201d \u201cWe\u2019ve got some things in common, both being from mid-major schools\u201d Hutchison said of Lillard. \u201cHe had to outwork a bunch of guys that were maybe recruited above him or got more hype than him. There are things I\u2019ve taken away from being around him\u2014how hard he works, his outlook on the game, on life. Seeing how he carries himself in everything he does, every decision he makes, even how he talks. He\u2019s just a complete professional. \u201cI\u2019ve got so much respect for him. He\u2019s shown me that, to get to where you want to go, you\u2019ve got to put the time in. You\u2019ve got to be willing to outwork everybody else. When I say I have no choice, I really mean it. This is the path I\u2019m on. I have no other choice.\u201d * * * Chris Dortch is the editor of the Blue Ribbon College Basketball Yearbook . Nice, but largely irrelevant. \u201cLot of years in the league,\u201d was Horford\u2019s go-to line after the Boston Celtics dismantled the rebuilding Chicago Bulls at United Center . \u201cYear 11. That\u2019s what happens when you play a lot of years.\u201d Horford sat down for the last time against Chicago with 4:07 left in the third quarter and his team leading by 37 points. He was a plus-31 in the game and became one of 16 active players to reach 10,000 points while averaging no more than 11.4 field-goal attempts. He\u2019s also the 14th in NBA history among players who were named to at least five All-Star teams. Horford and the Charlotte Hornets\u2019 Dwight Howard are the only two active players on that list. That economy of impact \u2014 scoring when needed, as part of an overall game \u2014 illustrates the value Horford has brought since his rookie season with the Atlanta Hawks in 2007-08. But it never has been more apparent than in the 146 games, regular and postseason, he has played for the Celtics since signing a four-year, $113 million free-agent deal with them in July 2016. That seemed awfully pricey for a guy who had averaged more than 18 points or 10 rebounds once each in his first nine seasons. But Boston improved from 48 victories and a first-round exit in 2015-16 to 53 and the Eastern Conference finals last season. This time, the Celtics are on pace to win 57, with playoff ambitions to match or top 2017\u2019s. At 12.8 points per game, Horford (who has scored 20 or more 10 times this season) only ranks fourth among Celtics scorers, averaging barely half of Kyrie Irving\u2019s 24.8 ppg. But it was that way a year ago, too, with Isaiah Thomas at 28.9 ppg and Horford at 14.0 ppg. In fact, one can make the case that Horford prefers it so, allowing him to contribute in a multitude of ways while still commanding respect from opposing defenses \u2014 and obviously, All-Star reserve votes from the conference\u2019s coaches. His net rating is 7.1, compared to Irving\u2019s 4.9. \u201cIf Al is open, we\u2019re going to get him the ball,\u201d Celtics coach Brad Stevens said. \u201cIf Al is at the rim, we want to get him the ball. But Al is also OK being a facilitator and making plays for everybody else. \u201cAl is a lot more concerned with how our team plays than his stat line.\u201d Even when Horford strung together some meager stats lines after the All-Star break \u2014 three points at Detroit, five points each against Memphis and Charlotte \u2014 Boston still won. It is 5-1 since the break, 2 1\/2 games behind the Toronto Raptors for top spot in the East \u2026 and 6 1\/2 in front of third-place Cleveland. Those are the sort of numbers that get Horford\u2019s attention. \u201cI came to Boston for the opportunity to compete for a championship,\u201d he said on his way out of United Center. \u201cAs long as we\u2019re winning, that\u2019s what I care about. It\u2019s always been that way with me, but it\u2019s even more true now. \u201cKyrie\u2019s the leader of our team, the head of our team. And for me, it\u2019s just to make sure I\u2019m making things easy for him. Then when the team needs me to step up and score, I will. Otherwise I need to just defend.\u201d Don\u2019t be fooled \u2014 Horford can exploit defensive mismatches and lapses, and rise to the proper occasion (he had 21 points, nine rebounds and 10 assists in Game 1 of the 2017 Eastern Conference semifinals and 15-6-5 in the Game 7 clincher). But there are a dozen other things Horford does in the seams, on and especially off the court, to help steer the Celtics. Not the least of which is his presence as a grown-up in the room, so often underrated in this league. Horford was old beyond his years, a calming voice in Atlanta\u2019s 74 playoff games from 2008-16. He\u2019s that guy again, only more so. Consider Celtics guard Marcus Smart\u2019s appreciation of Horford\u2019s counsel. \u201cThis season for me has been up and down,\u201d Smart said. \u201cInjuries and things like that. He\u2019s just always been there. Always positive. You need that when you go through hard times. He\u2019s been coaching up our rookies, helping them along the way. It\u2019s tough being a rookie, especially on a good team. You get thrown into the fire, you need somebody like Al there to help you.\u201d Teammate Marcus Morris referred to Horford as \u201cthe ultimate vet.\u201d But like Smart, he didn\u2019t know much previously about Horford\u2019s personality or character. To Morris, Horford seemed a fairly non-descript opponent. Cleveland needed a major facelift at the trade deadline and got it, and the Cavaliers and their fans were delighted. Then some harsh reality set in after the All-Star break (mostly defensively) and the new toys didn\u2019t seem quite as shiny. As with most toys, though, the fun comes from imagination in using them, and that\u2019s what coach Tyronn Lue had forced on him by Thompson\u2019s ankle injury. LeBron James and Nance Jr. have some chemistry on the court, fueled by the new guy\u2019s liveliness. Long-term, the Cavs\u2019 need for sugar rushes might not serve them so well through a long, grueling postseason but for now, Nance Jr. starting at center is what they need. Tas Melas :  Better but worse. Thompson needs to eat minutes in the Cavs\u2019 thin frontcourt rotation and despite Nance Jr.\u2019s good play, those minutes are better served as a starter. He is a true center, pushing Kevin Love to his proper spot at the 4, he\u2019s a vet who has started 54 straight playoff games with LeBron (LeBron loves his vets), and he achieves more with better players. Thompson wouldn\u2019t be as good off the bench \u2014 where Nance Jr. thrives \u2014 and Nance Jr. can finish games if the matchup dictates. Shaun Powell : More athletic and exciting. Plus, he hasn\u2019t reached his full potential. He\u2019s a consistent jump shot away from being a very good player. Thompson seems to be missing something; his impact games are becoming more scarce. He also hasn\u2019t evolved as a player or erased any of his weaknesses. His head has touched his ceiling and there\u2019s only one way to go from here. John Schuhmann :  Better. Thompson\u2019s primary job is to be an impact defender, and he hasn\u2019t been that this season. The Cavs have ranked in the bottom five defensively all season, and Thompson\u2019s rim protection numbers ( opponents have shot 70 percent at the rim when he\u2019s been there to protect it ) have been much worse than they\u2019ve been in previous seasons ( 60 percent in 2014-15 , 58 percent in \u201915-16 , and 55 percent last season ). Nance was part of a top-12 defense in L.A. and over the nine games with their new players, the Cavs have almost 17 points per 100 possessions better defensively with Nance on the floor than they\u2019ve been with him off the floor . That number might go down with him in the starting lineup, but it will be interesting to see how well the Cavs defend going forward and which one of these guys sees more playing time in the postseason with Kevin Love healthy.  Sekou Smith :  Fun and clearly more active above the rim, but still flawed. It\u2019s not a knock on Nance Jr., who has done nothing but play his role to perfection since the trade deadline. That still could have happened if they had stayed together, right?  * * * Steve Aschburner : No, it wouldn\u2019t have happened and this question raises a good point. In a league that has half as many superstars as it has franchises, it is a good thing when elite players seek out (or wind up on) their \u201cown\u201d teams and spread the talent around. That\u2019s why Harden blossoming as an MVP candidate and future Hall of Famer in ways he might not have had he stayed with the Thunder has been a boost not just to the Houston Rockets, but also to the league. It\u2019s why people are intrigued, for instance, about Klay Thompson\u2019s ability to be an A-lister elsewhere rather than a third- or fourth-wheel with Golden State. It\u2019s also why Durant joining the \u201c1-percenter\u201d Warriors irritated and annoyed so many. That said, we got teased with that original OKC3 in the 2012 Finals , then saw them pre-empted before they ever reached their potential. That, too, is something for which NBA fans root. Yet to Harden, per The Associated Press, he had a blunt answer when asked what Houston\u2019s win streak means to him. \u201c\u2018Nothing,\u201d he said. \u201dNothing at all. We just want to play well. We want to play well and have each other\u2019s back, no matter what, on both ends of the floor. It doesn\u2019t matter. Wins and losses will come.\u201d Yet the Rockets aren\u2019t the only team in the West getting attention of late. The New Orleans Pelicans are surging, having won nine straight games behind the play of All-Star big man Anthony Davis . In last night\u2019s showdown with the playoff-hopeful LA Clippers, Davis went off once again, logging 41 points, 13 rebounds, three steals and three blocks in a 121-116 New Orleans win . He scored 31 of those points in the second half, as he left the game in the second quarter with a rib contusion. \u201cDeMarcus [Cousins] told me at halftime, he said if you\u2019re not going back in, let me get your Achilles,\u201d Davis told the Players Only crew after Tuesday\u2019s game. Davis has been a one-man wrecking crew during this run, as he has scored no fewer than 23 points in a game during this win streak. He\u2019s averaging 37.7 points, 14.6 rebounds, 2.8 steals and three blocks per game while shooting 53.2 percent overall and 41.9 percent on 3-pointers during the nine-game win streak. He also has six games of 35-plus points during that span . Perhaps most key, though, is that the Pelicans are 8-0 this season when Davis logs 40 or more points in a game. \u201cHe is just playing on a really high level and nothing seems to affect him,\u201d New Orleans coach Alvin Gentry said of Davis. \u201cThat is a really tough (rib) injury right there. It feels like somebody is sticking an icepick in your side when you are trying to breathe with those bruised ribs and stuff like that. But he played through it and did a great job.\u201d The win keeps New Orleans in the chase for the No. 3 seed, which is held by the Portland Trail Blazers. They\u2019ve been making noise as well, with an All-Star of their own leading the charge. Damian Lillard dropped 37 points on the visiting New York Knicks last night in a 111-87 Blazers romp . Much like Davis, Lillard has put his team on his back and done a yeoman\u2019s share of the work as the Blazers have won eight in a row. Portland\u2019s eight-game winning streak marks its longest since Nov. 9-26, 2014 as the Blazers grew their lead in the Northwest Division to 1 1\/2 games. During this streak \u2014 which began on Valentine\u2019s Day \u2014 Lillard has given Portland fans reason after reason to love their go-to guy. He\u2019s averaging 33.1 ppg, 4.1 rpg, 5.8 apg and 1.3 spg while shooting 47.1 percent overall and 41.8 percent on 3-pointers during the win streak , which included victories against teams like the Oklahoma City Thunder, Minnesota Timberwolves, Utah Jazz and Golden State Warriors. Lillard made team history during the streak as well. He has now scored 354 points over the past 10 games, more than any Trail Blazer has scored in a 10-game span in team history. And for good measure, Lillard further etched his place in team history last night. First, he passed Cliff Robinson for No. 4 on the team\u2019s all-time scoring list and by game\u2019s end, had passed former teammate LaMarcus Aldridge for third on the team\u2019s all-time free throws made list . Per ESPN Stats & Information, Tuesday marked Lillard\u2019s 11th 35-point game of the season, which ties him for the most he had in any season of his career. \u201cWe\u2019ve been on a good run, just playing good basketball on both ends of the floor,\u201d Lillard said. \u201cOur team has been on a string; we\u2019ve been really connected.\u201d \u201cDame was just in a great groove,\u201d Blazers coach Terry Stotts said last night. \u201cHe\u2019s been in a groove for awhile. He was shooting it easy, feeling confident.\u201d"},{"id":41466,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/are-pistons-playoff-bound-stan-van-gundy-hot-seat","date":"2018-03-07","title":"Are Pistons playoff bound? That's not the only question looming in Detroit","content":" If he weren\u2019t coaching the Pistons, Stan Van Gundy could run for office in Detroit and probably win. His personality, his nature, his political leanings and his connection with the everyday man and woman meshes with a no-nonsense city that deserves strong leadership but rarely gets it. Pull up a chair and Van Gundy, approachable and magnetic, will sermonize on the evils and hypocrisy of society as well as sports, delivering with a common-sense style that will make you wonder why all people in authority aren\u2019t this free of agendas and conflicts of interest. The problem is, Van Gundy does coach the plummeting Pistons, and as team president, he drives them as well. His approval rating therefore is slippery, along with his grip on both jobs based on the dire circumstances that he and the Pistons currently find themselves in. They\u2019re running out of time and excuses for not making the playoffs, a real possibility with 18 games left in the regular season. The man responsible for this is hearing the music in Detroit and it isn\u2019t Smokey Robinson. Of all the playoff contenders in the NBA, is anyone on skates quite like the Pistons? At one point they were 14-6, now they\u2019re nearly five games out of the eighth and final spot in the East. Also, they\u2019ve won just one road game since mid-December and, uh-oh, there\u2019s a six-game Western trip starting next week. They\u2019re backpedaling here in the stretch run and fumbling to stop the slide, losing to the likes of the Magic and Hornets and fresh from a 22-point lashing courtesy of the Cavaliers, who have their own issues. The Pistons\u2019 play has often looked lethargic and uninspiring and other than Blake Griffin and Andre Drummond, the performances are lacking. Speaking of Griffin, his arrival from last month\u2019s blockbuster trade was supposed to awaken the club and a skeptical fan base that\u2019s not exactly stampeding through the doors of the new Little Caesars Arena. Yet, after an initial splash, the opposite has happened; the Pistons have lost nine out of 11 games, and six of seven since the All-Star break. They\u2019re lost. \u201cI know we\u2019re better and have better players than what\u2019s happening right now,\u201d Van Gundy said. Overall, this presents a murky picture for a team created and coached by Van Gundy, who\u2019s in the fourth of a five-year deal. It could also spell the end of coaches doubling as grand pooh-bahs, with Van Gundy dangerously on pace to copy the fate of Clippers coach Doc Rivers, who was stripped of his front office stripes last summer. Actually, if the Pistons keep this up, losing one job but not both would be a victory of sorts for Van Gundy. And so you\u2019re compelled to ask: What in the heck happened? What began as an uplifting and bold hire by new owner Tom Gores in 2014 is in jeopardy of collapsing. At the time, Van Gundy was out of the game, healing from an awkward and public fallout with Dwight Howard in Orlando, yet still held a degree of leverage. His coaching chops were very much intact and respected and the view around the league was Van Gundy received a raw deal from the Magic, who reached the NBA Finals on his Rolex. Therefore, he was in demand with each opening. But there was a catch. Van Gundy sought power, if only to avoid any repeat of the Howard fiasco. This was understandable from a guy who felt burned by the higher-ups at his old gig. He could build his team in his vision, without interference from above, without worrying about the resident star player pulling rank and going over his head in the event of a beef. Well, the Pistons were desperate when Gores bought the team and ousted Joe Dumars, who struggled to piece together a solid roster in his final few years. The Pistons had Ben Gordon and Charlie Villanueva and Josh Smith, all making big money, none making a big difference. Once the pride of the Eastern Conference, they hadn\u2019t won a playoff game in six years, hadn\u2019t made the playoffs in five. Gores dangled both jobs and Van Gundy jumped at the chance. He was hailed as a savior the moment the ink dried. Van Gundy inherited a wreck and needed time to open the windows and let the stink out. With the help of trusty GM Jeff Bower, he scrubbed the Pistons clean of Dumars\u2019 moves quickly, salvaging only Drummond. But the results and the decisions have since been a mixed bag, at best. He hasn\u2019t yet taken advantage of the surest way to find a franchise player, through the draft, and whiffed on two golden opportunities. Van Gundy took Stanley Johnson and Luke Kennard over Devin Booker and Donovan Mitchell. Those are lopsided decisions that haunt teams and set them back or stagnate them. Free agency hasn\u2019t been much better. Van Gundy gave $42 million to Jon Leuer, a role player when healthy. Another $21 million went to Boban Marjanovic; Van Gundy mostly kept him benched before tossing him into the Griffin deal. The trades are keeping the Pistons afloat, most notably getting Tobias Harris for virtually nothing, same for Reggie Jackson, and finally Griffin, a certified star and crowd pleaser who cost the Pistons a first-rounder, Harris and Avery Bradley. Collectively, Van Gundy received more than what he spent in those deals.  Jackson\u2019s time in Detroit is marked by solid play and plenty of pain. It\u2019s possible they wouldn\u2019t be in this bind if Jackson were healthy; he\u2019s working his way back from an ankle sprain that felled him during the holidays. Once he returns, and the timetable remains unclear, he\u2019ll give the Pistons a third wheel next to Drummond and Griffin. About Griffin: His efficiency is falling and feeding hints that he probably left his best years in Los Angeles. In his first five years with the Clippers, Griffin shot nearly 53 percent and was a fixture in the paint. Since then, he\u2019s had injuries and also stretched his shooting range, which certainly contributes to what we see now. Griffin\u2019s down to 42 percent this year, and while he\u2019s more confident from 18 feet and beyond, he needs more shots, too. He\u2019s only 28 and still someone who commands the respect of a double team. Also, he and Drummond are pairing up nicely so far and already developing on the same wavelength. The only potential worry lies more with his contract. His salaries the next four seasons, in millions: 31.8, 34, 36, 39. The Pistons are on the hook for that. For a player with a history of injuries (most were freakish in nature), that future money could be problematic. Also: Will Griffin fulfill another promise and help fill the empty seats in Detroit? That\u2019s partly why Van Gundy pulled off the deal, to give the Pistons someone worth the price of admission. Well: The Pistons are operating at 82 percent capacity, second-lowest to the Hawks. A team with the eighth-highest payroll is currently on the outside of the playoff bubble and struggles to sell tickets. Here\u2019s what\u2019s in Van Gundy\u2019s favor: He hasn\u2019t had a full season with Griffin and perhaps deserves one. Also, Gores likes him. Gores is a different kind of owner; he lives in Los Angeles and spends time with his private equity firm. He\u2019s mainly a ghost in Detroit and hands-off with the basketball operation. There is, however, Arn Tellem, the former ace agent who\u2019s now the Pistons\u2019 vice chairman. Surely, Gores will huddle up with Tellem this summer before weighing in on Van Gundy. It\u2019s possible Tellem could assume control of the basketball operation, much like other agents who\u2019ve made the jump to the other side with the Suns, Lakers and Warriors. Because Van Gundy has only one year left on the deal, and teams rarely allow coaches or executives to reach lame-duck status, something\u2019s bound to happen one way or another this offseason. There\u2019s still hope for the playoffs, however faint. Jackson will eventually return to form Lob (Motor) City, fortunes can change abruptly, and if they find themselves back in the mix, the Pistons close out with three of four games against lightweights. They need to make the playoffs to raise the possibility of zero happening to Van Gundy. Not surprisingly, Van Gundy isn\u2019t feeding speculation by even addressing the topic of his future. He\u2019s busy scratching his head and just trying to comprehend the present, much like everyone else. And like any responsible man in charge, he owns up. \u201cI\u2019ve got confidence in those guys and they should be able to play better than they are, and that\u2019s what gets you as a coach,\u201d Van Gundy said. \u201cI got to take the responsibility. I\u2019m obviously not getting us the right shots for the right people and I\u2019m not finding the answers. I\u2019m not leaving it on them.\u201d Veteran NBA writer Shaun Powell has worked for newspapers and other publications for more than 25 years. Draymond Green chopped it up in the locker room with James Harden. Harden and Steph Curry playfully re-enacted some of their favorite killer crossover moves. Klay Thompson put an arm around Mike D\u2019Antoni and squeezed. Good vibes all around. But this was a few weeks ago at the NBA All-Star Game , where selected Warriors and Rockets were on the same bench and page if for only a day. If the Rockets and Warriors meet again \u2014 and their paths in the Western Conference are indeed headed toward a postseason intersection \u2014 there will be a fight, in the basketball sense. That\u2019s because they\u2019ve distanced themselves from everyone else while enjoying each other\u2019s close company all season. Too close for comfort, perhaps? The intrigue in the West, if not the entire NBA, is dominated by two teams who can\u2019t shake one another and maybe never will until late May. There are roughly six weeks remaining in the regular season and this much is pretty clear: The Warriors are facing their biggest conference threat since creating this dynasty four years ago. The Rockets need to secure the best record and home-court advantage throughout the playoffs more than Golden State. And if basketball was fair, these teams would meet in the NBA Finals instead of one being left out. The Rockets, with a pair of 14-game winning streaks, have created the perception of being good enough to beat the Warriors, and the Warriors have looked vulnerable enough to raise this previously-unthinkable possibility just the slightest. Their hand-holding sprint to the regular-season finish and pending collision course at the Western Conference finals is the best drama going in the NBA outside of the Cavaliers. It\u2019ll be curious to see how two teams thriving mainly on 3-point shooting and creating chaos and supported by Kia MVP candidates settle the issue once and for all. \u201cWe\u2019re going to play hard, play for each other and the results are going to show,\u201d Harden said. \u201cYou can see how each individual works at his craft, whatever his craft is. We\u2019re not at a time to relax at all. We know how important this opportunity is. It\u2019s up to us to take advantage of everything coming our way and make the most of it.\u201d Yes, all the mystery mainly lies with the Rockets and whether they\u2019re for real as a title contender. We know about the Warriors. We\u2019re just now warming up to the Rockets. They\u2019re not bringing the two championships in three years or the track record of performance under pressure as the Warriors. By comparison, the Rockets are untested, unproven, more wishful. Yet: \u201cI think we have a serious chance,\u201d D\u2019Antoni said. The Rockets won two out of the three meetings with the Warriors this season; they\u2019re only the fourth team to beat the Warriors twice in a season since Steve Kerr became coach. They own the second-best offense, no surprise, and rated 10th defensively, a surprise. Of course, there\u2019s also Harden, who\u2019s pole-positioned to win the Kia MVP, arguably the best player in the NBA over the last three years after LeBron James. Harden has elevated himself as a must-see star who leads the NBA in scoring (31.2) and is third in assists (8.9) and has a 60-point triple double this season. Harden\u2019s impact in D\u2019Antoni\u2019s system can\u2019t be stressed enough, because it doesn\u2019t work unless he works. The ripple effect is ridiculous. His command of the double team makes Houston\u2019s dependence on the 3-pointer understandable, considering Eric Gordon, Trevor Ariza and Ryan Anderson all get an enviable share of open looks. How effective would they be if they needed to create the majority of their shots? Perhaps not nearly as much. Their value is inflated by Harden, at least in this system. Harden\u2019s dribble game and ability to shake defenders and reach the paint also produces layups for him or dunks for Clint Capela (65.5 percent field goal percentage); the defense can pick its poison. Those are the high percentage shots that give Houston another dimension and offensive balance. In all, the Rockets have seven players in double figures scoring and it\u2019s mostly due to Harden and the attention he gets. It\u2019s the true definition of making teammates better. Does it need to be mentioned that Harden, often a punch line when it comes to defense, is eighth in the league in steals ? Perhaps a reputation is being chopped down, at last. His bond with newcomer Chris Paul has been quick and problem-free, which is refreshing for Houston because of the often-tricky chemistry between ball-dominant stars in the past. Both made sacrifices to make it work by playing off the ball and showing mutual respect. And no starting backcourt in the NBA delivers more assists (17 per game), evidence of their instincts and willingness to share. It\u2019s a collaborative machine that squeezes the specific talents of everyone who checks into the game. \u201cThings are obviously going pretty good,\u201d D\u2019Antoni said. \u201cIt helps that we\u2019re in a race for the first seed. I think the guys enjoy coming into the locker room and playing. I don\u2019t think we\u2019re in a hurry for the season to get over with. It\u2019s been a great season so far and they\u2019ve enjoyed every day of it. I think the talk is, \u2018boy, this is going by really fast.\u2019 So if we can just make this last a little longer, it\u2019ll be great.\u201d  The Rockets are 32-1 with Paul, Harden and Capela on the floor together and overall have played only five games decided by three points or less. If you diminish the five-game losing streak during the holidays (Capela missed four of those games and Paul missed three), where would the Rockets be? Remember, they won 25 of their first 29. \u201cWe\u2019re worried about the Rockets and not anybody else,\u201d said D\u2019Antoni. The current 15-game win streak , Harden\u2019s MVP candidacy, Paul\u2019s arrival, 18 games with at least 19 made threes and improved defensive play are making the Rockets feel frisky. Two recent comments bear this out: Capella saying \u201cnow we know that we can definitely beat them\u201d \u2014 meaning the Warriors \u2014 on Jan. 20 and Harden\u2019s \u201cthis is the year, for sure\u201d declaration a week ago. When\u2019s the last time a team in the West were led by their chin and chest and genuinely felt they stood on equal ground with the Warriors during Golden State\u2019s current dynasty? In 2014-15, the Rockets finished second in the West but in truth were mismatched against the Warriors ; the harmony was prickly between Harden and Dwight Howard. The next season, the Spurs had a franchise-record 67 wins and added LaMarcus Aldridge and saw Kawhi Leonard become a blowout star, but they lost to Oklahoma City in the second round. The Thunder that year were well-equipped to handle the Warriors, and they did through the first four games of the West finals before Kevin Durant and Russell Westbrook blew a 3-1 lead . That series swung in Golden State\u2019s favor in a pair of ways; not only did the Warriors rally, but they also convinced Durant to sign up that summer. With Durant, the Warriors weren\u2019t threatened by anyone in the West last season, especially after the Spurs lost Leonard in the first game of their playoff series. But now the Rockets are not only back in the mix, they reloaded with Paul and an improved Capela and a better sense of the D\u2019Antoni system. Also, Gordon (18.7 points) is playing the best basketball of his life at age 29 and PJ Tucker was added last summer to bring a German Shepherd\u2019s attitude. Durant has noticed the difference, saying: \u201cThey\u2019re playing harder. And they\u2019re definitely playing defense harder than before.\u201d D\u2019Antoni knows the Rockets are at a disadvantage in terms of championship wisdom, something that\u2019s noticeably missing from Harden, who reached The Finals with OKC and played poorly in the series, and Paul, who hasn\u2019t advanced beyond the second round. He spoke lately about developing \u201cchampionship habits\u201d and believes winning will take care of that when and if the Rockets travel deep into the playoffs. He said: \u201cWe do have the talent and the ability to play and beat anybody at any time. We do have a goal in trying to win it. No shame in that. We also know Golden State\u2019s the best team. We still have some growing to do. They\u2019ve won the championship. We\u2019re confident, but at the same time, we know they\u2019ve done it.\u201d The Rockets are well on pace to post the best regular-season record in franchise history and yet that won\u2019t guarantee it\u2019ll come with best overall record in the West. The Warriors are still running in-step at the moment. April will determine how important it is to the Warriors, who could rest their starters more often than D\u2019Antoni will sit Harden and Paul. Again: Houston seemingly wants home-court more, and maybe needs it more. \u201cIt\u2019s important,\u201d Harden said. \u201cThat\u2019s why we\u2019re going to take it one step at a time and be the best that we can be.\u201d And the Warriors? They\u2019ve adopted the \u201ccatch us if you can\u201d attitude and placing a premium on staying healthy, first and foremost. Perhaps fortified by two championships in three years and the knowledge that any warts at the moment can be erased once the postseason begins, they rightly see themselves as the hunted, rather than the hunter, in the West. Coach Steve Kerr has harped on the Warriors\u2019 occasional defensive lapses and more than a few times this season wondered if the team is still responding to him, which led him to famously hand over the clipboard a week ago to his players during timeouts. Still, few in the basketball world are buying the idea of the Warriors being unmotivated or diminished. And consider this: Despite all the Houston win streaks, the Warriors are also at the top in the West. How much of a psychological blow would it be to Houston if the Warriors clinch best record? Nothing\u2019s changed with the Warriors, who still have four All-Stars, a pair of MVP candidates in Curry and Durant, and noted playoff beast Andre Iguodala is slowly awakening from his regular season hibernation. Curry compared the current Rockets\u2019 confidence to Golden State\u2019s mentality before the titles began rolling in. That\u2019s why he chuckled at all the fuss made over the bravado comments from Capela and Harden and asked, \u201cwhat else are (they) supposed to say?\u201d The Warriors don\u2019t discuss the Rockets as much as the Rockets are willing to discuss them. That\u2019s understandable. Yet the time could be fast approaching when the Warriors must concede the obvious and there\u2019s nobody else except Houston standing between them and a fourth trip to The Finals. Does anyone expect differently? Veteran NBA writer Shaun Powell has worked for newspapers and other publications for more than 25 years. "},{"id":47505,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/morning-tip-golden-state-warriors-showing-some-weakness-latest-title-run","date":"2018-03-05","title":"New era, new challenges to retaining throne awaits Golden State Warriors","content":" \u201cIt\u2019s the lack of faith that makes people afraid of meeting challenges, and I believe in myself. He who is not courageous enough to take risks will accomplish nothing in life. I figured that if I said it enough, I would convince the world that I really was the greatest.\u201d \u2014 Muhammad Ali Ali defended his heavyweight championship 20 times, during two eras: when he was young and unstoppable, after beating Sonny Liston in Miami in 1964, and when he was old and vulnerable, after beating George Foreman in Zaire in 1974. He was the fastest heavyweight ever in the first era; he was smart and could take a punch in the second. A generation later, the Golden State Warriors are defending their NBA title for a second time, in three years. But they, too, are doing so in two eras. In 2014, no one had seen anything like what Golden State did on a basketball court, and how Stephen Curry\u2019s and Klay Thompson\u2019s shooting range changed the geometry of NBA defenses . They stretched to the breaking point trying to get out to Curry and Thompson. They couldn\u2019t figure out how to handle the Warriors\u2019 five-man switching defenses. They couldn\u2019t stand up under Golden State\u2019s withering pace . There is no need to hold a telethon yet for the Warriors, three years later. They are 49-14 today , with four All-Stars among their five starters, including Kia MVP candidate Kevin Durant, in the prime of his career, who wasn\u2019t there when the Warriors first beat the Cleveland Cavaliers in the 2015 Finals . They are still first in the league in Offensive Rating , first in True Shooting Percentage , first in Effective Field Goal Percentage . They still are unsolvable to most opponents. But maybe not all, not anymore. The margin of separation between Golden State and the rest of the league is still there, most of the time. But there are tiny signs of slippage. Tiny. You recall what Warriors assistant coach Bruce Frasier said in the preseason, when no one is injured and everyone thinks they\u2019re going 82-0. \u201cTeams are starting to figure us out a little bit,\u201d he said then. \u201cWe\u2019re talented, so that sometimes overrides strategy. But I feel like teams are figuring certain things out to do to counter what they\u2019ve seen. Year one, it was really hard, because it was all new. The pieces have changed a little bit, but I feel like our challenge will be to see if we can layer on some of the offense, our fluid movement, and counters, and change things up, and execute better. Defense is always big, too, so I wouldn\u2019t go into the complacent (problem). I think it\u2019s going to be more execution, and how smart can we really be, and can we keep that energy up through this year?\u201d In each of their previous three seasons, the Warriors led the league in margin of victory \u2014 10.1 points in 2014-15 , 10.8 points in 2015-16 and 11.6 points last season . This year, though, they\u2019ve fallen to third, behind the Houston Rockets and Toronto Raptors \u2014 and their win margin is down to 8.5 points per game . Two years ago, the Warriors were fourth in the league in Defensive Rating (100.9) . Last season, Golden State was second (101.1) . This season, the Warriors are fifth, at 103.4 . In 2014-15, they were 14th in the league in points allowed in the paint ; this year, they\u2019re 24th (to be fair, they were 23rd last year , when they won it all anyway). Are they bored? Tired? Aging? Is their bench inconsistency this year the result of vets saving themselves for the playoffs, or guys just getting old? And will it matter against anyone other than Houston? \u201cOnce you start getting a little older, it\u2019s harder and harder,\u201d guard Shaun Livingston said last week. \u201cWe definitely need the youth, we definitely need the health. We\u2019ve got to be healthy. We\u2019ve got to be healthy. Sometimes you see teams that maybe are over the hill \u2014 they have the experience, but maybe not (the ability). It\u2019s human nature. Obviously, I don\u2019t think we\u2019re there yet. We\u2019ve got guys that are still in their prime. It\u2019s mental now.\u201d In the Jean-Pierre Coopman phase of their latest title defense (oh, how one misses spectacles like Ali fighting Coopman, the \u201cLion of Flanders\u201d \u2014 with Pat Summerall and Tom Brookshier on the call!), the Warriors came to Washington last week. There was no White House visit on the docket, only time with D.C. area kids and a trip to the African-American History Museum , with owner Joe Lacob and GM Bob Myers on the trip as well. They have been in the public eye for five years now, back to Mark Jackson\u2019s last season as coach, when the Splash Brothers exploded into the national consciousness . That\u2019s a long time for one NBA team to have all that light and heat on it. For a minute, the Warriors tried to convince themselves that there was a backlash building against them nationally, that people had grown tired of their 3-pointers and video game point totals. It was, of course, a ridiculous posit \u2014 Golden State and its players are more popular than ever, the love for Curry such that he felt perfectly comfortable posting a photo of the glass table he accidentally smashed in his hotel room on Instagram , any criticism surely to be muted amid America\u2019s love for the two-time MVP. https:\/\/www.instagram.com\/p\/Bfy7u2RgBlv\/?utm_source \u201cThere was a little guy who was probably eight years old, and he came up and introduced himself,\u201d Steve Kerr said. \u201cHis name was Ryan, and I\u2019m talking to him, and he goes \u2019oh, my God, there\u2019s Quinn Cook!\u2019 And he ran over to Quinn Cook. Not Steph, not me \u2014 he loved Quinn Cook. That was cool.\u201d Throughout the Warriors\u2019 run, they\u2019ve faced down different challengers in the Western Conference \u2014 the first iteration of the Rockets with Harden, a hybrid inside-out attack where Houston unhappily and unsuccesffully tried to meld Harden and Dwight Howard in the post . The Durant\/Russell Westbrook one-two combo in Oklahoma City. The Spurs, morphing from the Tim Duncan\/Tony Parker-led team to the Kawhi Leonard-dominant one. The \u201cLob City\u201d Clippers, followed by the Chris Paul\/Blake Griffin halfcourt version. But this season\u2019s Rockets, with Paul at the point, may be the most unique and dangerous threat to the Warriors. They are much more than a team that just rains 3-pointers on you \u2014 though they most certainly do that, and do it historically well. They\u2019re also an outstanding defensive team, with the additions of P.J. Tucker and Luc Mbah a Moute giving them a grit they haven\u2019t had in past seasons to pair with the shot blocking and rim presence of Clint Capela. The numbers are stark: Houston is 32-1 this season when Paul, Harden and Capela all play , including two wins over the Warriors. The Rockets have no obvious weakness. They have no fear of Golden State, either, having won two of the three meetings with the Warriors this season. It\u2019s not just that they\u2019re good, it\u2019s how they\u2019re good that makes them look like the greatest challenge yet to Golden State\u2019s hegemony in the West. \u201cI mean, yes, because they do it a different way, I guess,\u201d Curry said last week. \u201cThey adopted the power of the three ball and try to use it as a main weapon, and obviously with James and CP together. Honestly, we know that they\u2019re playing well. We\u2019re chasing that number one seed and keeping tabs on how they\u2019re playing and whatnot. But at the end of the day, we\u2019ve got a lot of time left before we have to face them again. We know they\u2019re serious. But so are we.\u201d The Warriors have had to deal with great adversity during their run, to be sure. The biggest challenge came about this time last year, when a collision between teammates \u2014 Zaza Pachulia and Durant, in D.C., ironically \u2014 culminated in a Grade 2 MCL sprain and bone bruise for Durant , taking him out of the lineup at the worst possible part of the season. Golden State had just ripped off wins in 23 of its previous 27 games since a lamentable Christmas Day loss to the Cavs . Curry had started to figure out how to play with KD, and vice versa. They were in the middle of a brutal stretch of seven road games in eight overall, with the one brief return home to play the Celtics. When Durant went down, the initial fear was that he\u2019d torn his ACL and would be out for the season. The Warriors\u2019 locker room was funeral after the Wizards game. \u201cObviously, we were trying to figure out if he was like \u2019done-done\u2019 for the year, or whether or not there was going to be a chance he\u2019d return,\u201d forward David West said. \u201cWe were, at the time he got hurt, we were just starting to figure out the sort of roles, everybody was getting comfortable with roles. We basically had to reset., change some of the functions we were doing. We lost a few games trying to literaly just figure out and recalibrate and re-balance. That was one of those periods where we were just looking at each other, trying to start this thing \u2014 we lost this huge, huge piece.\u201d Yet the Warriors figured it out on the fly. And how they responded then provides a big clue to how they might respond to the challenge the Rockets present to them now. \u201cIt took us, I think we needed to get home before we were able to stablize,\u201d Kerr said. \u201cI want to say we lost three of the last four on the trip or something (they did lose three of four, but one of the three losses was at Oracle in that one home game with the Celtics). We got home and righted the ship and got going. But sometimes (an injury is) a galvanizing force when a guy gets hurt, and you have to do certain things. Like, for us, when Kevin got hurt, we talked about it and we said we have to be the best defensive team in the league. We don\u2019t have that luxury of throwing the ball to Kevin and saying \u2019get us 30 points tonight.\u2019\u201d During that stretch without Durant (March 2, 2017 to April 5, 2017), who returned just before the start of the playoffs, the Warriors led the league in the league in Defensive Rating (100.0, just head of San Antonio\u2019s 100.2), first in opponent field goal percentage (.429), tied for second in opponent 3-point percentage (.316) and fourth in opponent points allowed per game (100.9). And once Durant returned for good, the Warriors again flexed. They tore through the West, winning all but one game en route to a third straight NBA Finals. And they took the Cavaliers apart in five games for their second title in three years. \u201cYou could see Draymond, Klay, Andre, Shaun, those guys, even Loon (Kevin Looney), were like, \u2019we didn\u2019t have KD last year,\u2019 \u201d West said. \u201cFor someone like myself, I just followed their lead. Klay got a little more aggressive. Draymond sort of settled everybody defensively. And we started winning.\u201d That muscle memory will come in handy this year. Durant and Curry have missed time with injuries, and Golden State hasn\u2019t figured out things at center just yet. (Would it shock me if rookie Jordan Bell played a big role there down the stretch? No, it would not.) But the Warriors still are smoking people in the second halves of games; per teamrankings.com, the Warriors lead the lead in third-quarter scoring margin at 5.3 points per game, more than double the margin of the second-place Denver Nuggets. Whether it\u2019s adjustments or something else (\u201cmainly, fiery halftime speeches, Knute Rockne style,\u201d Kerr opines), they have again put a lot of opponents away with 12 minutes to spare. Since the All-Star break, they\u2019re fourth in the league in opponent field goal percentage (.433) and Defensive Rating (100.3). \u201cThis year, obviously, knock on wood, we want to stay healthy,\u201d Curry said. \u201cWe want to continue to push in the right direction. Every year\u2019s different. That\u2019s the fun part about this league. No matter how much success you\u2019ve had and what your expectations are, it\u2019s a different journey every year. We\u2019re right in the middle of that right now. We have an amazing record, considering how we\u2019ve played. I think we\u2019d all say we haven\u2019t lived up to our own expectations. That\u2019s okay. We have an opportunity to build the right habits and the right momentum going into the playoffs this year and do it, all 15 guys.\u201d * * * Longtime NBA reporter, columnist and Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Famer David Aldridge is an analyst for TNT. That it came from the Twitter account of a four-time NBA All-Star, whose team was en route to the best season in franchise history, only added to the confusion. But there it was. \u201c This depression get the best of me\u2026\u201d DeMar DeRozan tweeted, and it surprised just about everyone, because the 28-year-old is pretty quiet most of the time. But DeRozan has been carrying a lot on his plate. Not only is trying to lead Toronto somewhere it\u2019s never been before, but has never has as a good a chance before, either \u2014 The Finals \u2014 but he\u2019s been doing it while going back and forth between Toronto and Los Angeles, where his father, Frank DeRozan, has been hospitalized for weeks. Frank DeRozan has been DeMar\u2019s biggest coach, biggest critic and biggest champion his whole life, never being satisfied as his son rose through the ranks of basketball, from Compton High to USC to the NBA. But Frank DeRozan has suffered health setbacks in recent years \u2014 a stroke and significant kidney problems, per the Toronto Sun \u2014 and DeMar has gone bicoastal multiple times to be with his dad, never missing a game in the process . (Frank DeRozan was able, though, to temporarily leave the hospital last month in L.A. to go to Staples Center to see DeMar play for Team Stephen in the All-Star Game.) In his ninth season in Toronto \u2014 he\u2019s never asked for a trade and agreed almost immediately to a $139 million extension with the Raptors in 2016, never even looking at free agency \u2014 DeRozan has scored less than he did last season, but is averaging a career-high 5.2 assists and gone all in on Toronto\u2019s \u201cculture reset,\u201d as GM Masai Ujiri put it after the Raptors went out again in the playoffs last year. After years of resisting, arguing not without merit that he was a master of the mid-range game, DeRozan has embraced the 3-pointer this season, obliterating his previous highs for attempts and makes behind the arc, and keeping the ball moving both to fellow All-Star Kyle Lowry and to the team\u2019s emerging cast of young, talented players, who\u2019ve helped carry the load all season. After winning Sunday, the Raptors are an Eastern Conference best 45-17, and are closing in on home court throughout the playoffs in the East. All would seem to be great. But, as DeRozan\u2019s social media statement made clear (and, to his credit, he acknowledged it was him and that he wasn\u2019t hacked, and he hasn\u2019t taken the Tweet down), life sometimes gets in the way of all our dreams. Me: So, your dad was able to come to Staples Center to see you at the All-Star Game. How was that for him? DeMar DeRozan: It was good. It was real good. He had a good time. It was cool for him to be able to come out and experience it and enjoy it. It made me feel good. He was happy about it. Me: And how is he doing? DD: Every day is one of them things where you just don\u2019t know until he\u2019s home. Until he gets home, that\u2019s when I think I\u2019ll be more comfortable, knowing, cool, you\u2019re out of there. He\u2019s been in there since Dec. 23. It\u2019s March 2nd. I know just that is bothering him, being in there and wanting to get out. Just on top of that, my mom, when I was home the other day, my mom was telling me \u2018this is the longest I\u2019ve been without my husband in 30-plus years.\u2019 Stuff like that, that\u2019s the rough part of it. Me: So is that where your head\u2019s at right now? DD: Without a doubt. For sure. One thing I always try to do whenever I go out there and play is try to do whatever I can, knowing I\u2019m so far, doing something I know will make them proud, make them feel good, give them a kind of energy. That\u2019s kind of where I\u2019ll be with it. Me: Is it hard to compartmentalize? So many people say the court is their refuge? DD: For me, it\u2019s easy to do, from the moment of playing to kind of lock in and focus and kind of indulge in that moment. It\u2019s crazy you say that, because Kyle, he\u2019s one of my closest friends, he knows me so well. A lot of times after the game, the first thing he\u2019ll say to me is \u2018back to reality.\u2019 He knows now our night is over. Now I have to go back and get into the reality of DeMar. It\u2019s crazy. Me: What have you heard from folks since you sent that tweet out? DD: Man, where haven\u2019t I heard from? Honestly, the response, I can honestly say that I wouldn\u2019t have even thought how the response, how it came out, I wouldn\u2019t have thought I\u2019d ever gotten anything like that. Especially me. I\u2019ve never been one who wanted any type of attention, good nor bad. The response I got from people was so uplifting, positive, refreshing. It\u2019s crazy. It\u2019s crazy. But it made me feel good. You just look at certain things. People say \u2018you helped me. Because if you\u2019re going through something like this, I can get through it.\u2019 It\u2019s incredible. By far one of the most incredible things in my career that I\u2019ve witnessed outside of basketball. Me: So you could be a role model in a whole different way. DD: For sure. I never looked at myself and said \u2018man, I want to be a role model.\u2019 But something like that is extremely important. It\u2019s all walks of life. I done had high school players, college players, older people. I had one older coach that I\u2019ve known text me and tell me, \u2018if there was a player when I was young that I\u2019d seen or witnessed who was going through something (like this), it would have helped me \u2014 then \u2014 not be an alcoholic.\u2019 It was incredible to hear words like that. It\u2019s been one of them things where I\u2019m like, \u2018damn, I\u2019m just speaking the truth.\u2019 It\u2019s crazy. Me: Is there anything you\u2019re doing formally or officially now to deal with it? DD: Nah. I think I\u2019m going to definitely, once we\u2019re all said and done, probably the summertime for sure, I\u2019ll be open arms about it without a doubt. At the end of the day, it\u2019s like it\u2019s one of them things where you can\u2019t play basketball forever, but if there\u2019s something I can do that will outlast it and be helpful, be bigger than basketball, I\u2019m all for it. It\u2019s life. Me: So y\u2019all are in this new position on top of the East. You\u2019ve been good for a minute over the years, but this is the top of the top. Is the vibe different in the locker room? DD: Definitely. It\u2019s more, we have fun with one another, but we understand it\u2019s bigger than us all. We, all of us \u2014 young guys, all of me. Me and Kyle always tell the young guys, \u2018this opportunity doesn\u2019t always come around that often. Take advantage of this and be all for it. Before you know it, you\u2019re going to be 10 years in, and the opportunity may not come again. Take full advantage of it.\u2019 And everybody understands that. We see it now, especially when we have games where we lose a game. We think we\u2019re on a 10-game losing streak. That\u2019s how we approach coming in the next day at practice, or the next game. It\u2019s great to have that kind of feeling and vibe. Me: How do you know when you\u2019re all locked in? DD: You just know. I always look at my guy Kyle, and you know he\u2019s gonna ride or die with you. But it\u2019s crazy when you\u2019re able to look over at a guy like Pascal (Siakam), or Freddie (Van Vleet), or Delon (Wright), these young guys who only have a couple of years in the league, they\u2019ve got the same look that Kyle\u2019s got. That says a lot about the team. Because you know when those young guys go in, they\u2019re some dogs, too. That\u2019s the beauty of it, and it shows. Me: So, about those young guys. You know what you\u2019re gonna do in the playoffs, and you know what Kyle\u2019s gonna do, and Jo. But if you\u2019re going to beat an elite team in the playoffs, the young guys are gonna have to perform. DD: Yeah. And they have. I lost count of how many games our starters haven\u2019t even played in the fourth quarter. Against good teams, not just lower teams. There have been times where we\u2019re playing some great teams, and the coaches come in and look at us, and we\u2019re like, \u2018nah, let them finish out the game. They\u2019ve got this.\u2019 It\u2019s great to have that type of confidence in the young guys. It\u2019s amazing. I know we get a lot of credit, but they deserve just as much credit.
